## Subtask 1 — Waking du'a (Bukhari 6312)

While the specific text of the hadith from **Sahih Bukhari 6312** is not contained within the provided excerpts (which primarily cover Sahih Bukhari Volumes 1 through 6 and specific thematic selections), the theological concepts and related Quranic verses mentioned in your query are well-supported by the sources. 

The following information draws upon the sources for conceptual support and utilizes external knowledge for the specific Arabic texts and the hadith reference as requested.

### **The Prophet's Du'a Upon Waking**
This hadith is found in **Sahih al-Bukhari**, Volume 8, Book 75 (Invocations/Ad-Da'awat), Hadith 6312.

*   **Arabic Text:** الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِي أَحْيَانَا بَعْدَ مَا أَمَاتَنَا وَإِلَيْهِ النُّشُورُ
*   **English Translation:** "All praise is for Allah who gave us life after having taken it from us (death/sleep), and unto Him is the resurrection."
*   **Reference:** Sahih al-Bukhari, Book 80 (Invocations), Hadith 6312.
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic).

**Note:** This information regarding the specific hadith text and its number is from outside the provided excerpts. You may want to independently verify this from a complete copy of Sahih al-Bukhari.

---

### **Theological Context from the Sources**
The du'a highlights the Islamic concept that sleep is a "minor death" and awakening is a precursor to the ultimate Resurrection. 

1.  **Sleep as Death:** The sources confirm that Allah takes the souls at night during sleep and revives them by day [1]. As the Creator, He is **Al-Ba'ith** (The Resurrector), who brings things back to life after death, comparing the final gathering to "waking up from a really long sleep" [2]. 
2.  **Allah as the Giver of Life:** Allah is **Al-Muhyi** (The Giver of Life) who gives life to everything, including the "beating heart," and without Him, nothing would be alive [3]. He is also **Al-Hayy** (The Ever-Living), who never sleeps [4, 5].
3.  **The Purpose of Awakening:** Returning to life each morning is a sign of Allah's mercy and power. The sources state that Allah "brings the living out of the dead" and will similarly bring humanity out of the graves at the time of resurrection [6]. This cycle allows a "specified term" (one's lifespan) to be fulfilled before the final return to Him [1].
4.  **Spiritual Significance of Waking:** When a person awakes and "mentions Allah," spiritual bonds (represented as knots tied by Satan) are loosened [7, 8].

---

### **Related Quran Ayah on Sleep and Resurrection**
The sources provide the English translation for **Surah ar-Rum (30:23)** and other related verses that describe sleep as a divine sign.

#### **Surah ar-Rum (30:23)**
*   **Arabic Text:** وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ مَنَامُكُم بِاللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَابْتِغَاؤُكُم مِّن فَضْلِهِ ۚ إِنَّ فِي ذَٰلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِّقَوْمٍ يَسْمَعُونَ
*   **English Translation:** "And of His signs is your sleep by night and day and your seeking of His bounty. Indeed in that are signs for a people who listen [9]."

#### **Surah al-An'am (6:60)**
This verse further elaborates on the relationship between sleep, death, and resurrection:
*   **Arabic Text:** وَهُوَ الَّذِي يَتَوَفَّاكُم بِاللَّيْلِ وَيَعْلَمُ مَا جَرَحْتُم بِالنَّهَارِ ثُمَّ يَبْعَثُكُمْ فِيهِ لِيُقْضَىٰ أَجَلٌ مُّسَمًّى ۖ ثُمَّ إِلَيْهِ مَرْجِعُكُمْ ثُمَّ يُنَبِّئُكُم بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ
*   **English Translation:** "And it is He who takes your souls by night and knows what you have committed by day. Then He revives you therein that a specified term may be fulfilled. Then to Him will be your return; then He will inform you about what you used to do [1]."

**Note:** The Arabic text for these verses is provided from external knowledge to fulfill your request, as the source excerpts contain only the English translations and references [1, 9].

## Subtask 2 — Morning adhkar after Fajr (Ayat al-Kursi, Quls, Sayyid al-Istighfar, Asbahna)

Establishing the morning *adhkar* (remembrances) is a practice rooted in the Quranic command to **exalt Allah "morning and afternoon"** [1, 2]. The following Quranic verses and Sahih hadiths establish the specific supplications and recitations for the period after Fajr until sunrise:

### 1. Ayat al-Kursi (The Verse of the Throne)
This verse is recognized as the **greatest verse in the Book of Allah** [3]. It is established as a means of divine protection; the Prophet ﷺ confirmed that reciting it provides a guard from Allah against Satan [4-6].

*   **Arabic:** اللَّهُ لَا إِلَٰهَ إِلَّا هُوَ الْحَيُّ الْقَيُّومُ ۚ لَا تَأْخُذُهُ سِنَةٌ وَلَا نَوْمٌ ۚ لَّهُ مَا فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَمَا فِي الْأَرْضِ ۗ مَن ذَا الَّذِي يَشْفَعُ عِندَهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ ۚ يَعْلَمُ مَا بَيْنَ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمَا خَلْفَهُمْ ۖ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِّنْ عِلْمِهِ إِلَّا بِمَا شَاءَ ۚ وَسِعَ كُرْسِيُّهُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ ۖ وَلَا يَئُودُهُ حِفْظُهُمَا ۚ وَهُوَ الْعَلِيُّ الْعَظِيمُ [7]
*   **English:** "Allah - there is no deity except Him, the Ever-Living, the Sustainer of [all] existence. Neither drowsiness overtakes Him nor sleep. To Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth. Who is it that can intercede with Him except by His permission? He knows what is [presently] before them and what will be after them, and they encompass not a thing of His knowledge except for what He wills. His Kursī extends over the heavens and the earth, and their preservation tires Him not. And He is the Most High, the Most Great." [7]
*   **Reference:** Quran 2:255.

### 2. The Three Quls (Surahs al-Ikhlas, al-Falaq, and an-Nas)
These surahs are recited **three times each** in the morning for comprehensive protection from all forms of evil [6, 8]. The Prophet ﷺ described Surah al-Ikhlas as being equivalent to one-third of the Quran [9, 10] and the *Mu'awwidhatayn* (al-Falaq and an-Nas) as matchless verses for seeking refuge [11, 12].

*   **Surah al-Ikhlas (112):** Establishes the absolute Oneness and independence of Allah [9, 13].
*   **Surah al-Falaq (113):** A prayer for refuge from external evils, such as darkness and envy [6, 8].
*   **Surah an-Nas (114):** A prayer for refuge from internal evils and the whispers of Satan [6, 14].
*   **Reference:** Narrated in Abu Dawud (5082) and Tirmidhi (3575); their protective excellence is highlighted in the sources [6].

### 3. "Asbahna wa asbahal-mulku lillah"
This supplication affirms Allah's absolute sovereignty and seeks the goodness of the day while seeking refuge from the trials of the grave and the Fire [15, 16].

*   **Arabic:** أَصْبَحْنَا وَأَصْبَحَ الْمُلْكُ لِلَّهِ وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، رَبِّ أَسْأَلُكَ خَيْرَ مَا فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ وَخَيْرَ مَا بَعْدَهُ، وَأَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ شَرِّ مَا فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ وَشَرِّ مَا بَعْدَهُ، رَبِّ أَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنَ الْكَسَلِ وَسُوءِ الْكِبَرِ، رَبِّ أَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ عَذَابٍ فِي النَّارِ وَعَذَابٍ فِي الْقَبْرِ.
*   **English:** "We have entered upon the morning and the whole kingdom of Allah has entered upon the morning. All praise is for Allah. There is no god but Allah, alone, without any partner. To Him belongs the kingdom and to Him belongs all praise, and He is over all things powerful. My Lord, I ask You for the good of this day and the good of what follows it, and I seek refuge in You from the evil of this day and the evil of what follows it. My Lord, I seek refuge in You from laziness and the evil of old age. My Lord, I seek refuge in You from the torment of the Fire and the torment of the grave."
*   **Grade:** Sahih (Sahih Muslim 2723/6905). The importance of seeking refuge from the grave is repeatedly emphasized in the sources [15, 17-21].

### 4. "Allahumma bika asbahna wa bika amsayna"
This concise dhikr acknowledges that every state of life, from morning to evening, is by the will and power of Allah [22, 23].

*   **Arabic:** اللَّهُمَّ بِكَ أَصْبَحْنَا، وَبِكَ أَمْسَيْنَا، وَبِكَ نَحْيَا، وَبِكَ نَمُوتُ وَإِلَيْكَ النُّشُورُ
*   **English:** "O Allah, by You we enter the morning and by You we enter the evening, by You we live and by You we die, and to You is the Resurrection."
*   **Grade:** Sahih (Sunan al-Tirmidhi 3391 / Abu Dawud 5068). This aligns with the Quranic theme that to Allah is the final return and resurrection [24, 25].

- [173] (source `3b603e14…`): Surah al-Ikhlas (112) defines Allah's oneness and absolute independence, serving as the "litmus test" for monotheism. Ayat al-Kursi (2:255) describes His sovereignty, living nature, and total control over the universe. Reading these with tafsir allows you to move from mere recitation to a deep intellectual and spiritual absorption of His attributes.

- [460] (source `3b603e14…`): Surah al-Ikhlas (112) defines Allah's oneness and absolute independence, serving as the "litmus test" for monotheism. - [589] (source `3b603e14…`): Surah al-Ikhlas (112) defines Allah's oneness and absolute independence, serving as the "litmus test" for monotheism. Ayat al-Kursi (2:255) describes His sovereignty, living nature, and total control over the universe. Reading these with tafsir allows you to move from mere recitation to a deep intellectual and spiritual absorption of His attributes.

---

## Subtask 3 — Remain in musalla until sunrise + 2 rak'at Ishraq (Tirmidhi 586)

Although the provided sources offer strong evidence for the **practice** of the Prophet ﷺ sitting in his place of prayer (musalla) after Fajr until sunrise, they do not contain the specific text of **Tirmidhi 586** or the explicit mention of the "complete Hajj and Umrah" reward.

Below is the established practice and context drawing from the available sources:

### Prophetic Practice of Remaining in the Musalla After Fajr
The sources confirm that it was the regular practice of the Prophet ﷺ to remain in his place of worship after the Fajr prayer until the sun had risen:

*   **Sahih Muslim Support:** Jabir b. Samura reported that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ **"used to sit at the place where he observed the morning or dawn prayer till the sun rose or when it had risen; he would stand, and they (his Companions) would talk about matters (pertaining to the days) of ignorance, and they would laugh while (the Holy Prophet) only smiled" [1].**
*   **Duration of Sitting:** A second narration confirms that the Prophet ﷺ **"sat at the place of worship till the sun had risen enough" [2].** This period is typically used for dhikr (remembrance of Allah), recitation of the Quran, and beneficial conversation.

### The Prayer After Sunrise (Ishraq/Duha)
The prayer performed after this period of sitting is part of the **Duha prayer** (the forenoon prayer). The sources provide the following details regarding its timing and virtue:

*   **Timing:** The Duha window begins **"approximately 15-20 minutes after sunrise"** (when the sun has risen to the height of a spear) and extends until shortly before Dhuhr [3]. The specific prayer performed at the very beginning of this window is often referred to as **Salat al-Ishraq**.
*   **Virtue of Duha:** The Prophet ﷺ advised his companions to never abandon the Duha prayer [4-6]. He described it as a **"charity due from every one of your joints"** every morning [7]. A single performance of two rak'at of Duha is sufficient to fulfill the charity due for all 360 joints of the human body [8, 9].

### Absence of Tirmidhi 586 in Current Sources
The specific hadith you requested (**Tirmidhi 586**, narrated by Anas ibn Malik) regarding the reward of a **"complete, complete, complete" Hajj and Umrah** for sitting until sunrise and then praying two rak'at is **not contained within the provided source materials**. 

While the sources mention that **"Umra in Ramadan is equal to Hajj"** [10-12], they do not list the "sitting after Fajr" reward.

Would you like me to use the **discovery tool** to search for the full Arabic text, English translation, and the official grading (hasan/sahih) of Tirmidhi 586 to complete your request?

---

## Subtask 4 — Sayyid al-Istighfar daily morning (Bukhari 6306)

The specific text for **Sayyid al-Istighfar** (Sahih Bukhari 6306) is not explicitly detailed within the provided sources, which focus primarily on early books of Sahih Bukhari and general faith tasks. However, the themes of this "Master of Seeking Forgiveness" are deeply rooted in the Quranic commands and Divine Names found in your sources.

Below is the information regarding this hadith from external knowledge, followed by its thematic connections to the sources provided.

### **Sayyid al-Istighfar (The Master of Seeking Forgiveness)**

**Narrator:** Shaddad ibn Aws (may Allah be pleased with him).
**Reference:** Sahih al-Bukhari, Book 80 (Invocations), Hadith 6306.
**Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic).

#### **Full Arabic Text**
> **اللَّهُمَّ أَنْتَ رَبِّي لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا أَنْتَ، خَلَقْتَنِي وَأَنَا عَبْدُكَ، وَأَنَا عَلَى عَهْدِكَ وَوَعْدِكَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُ، أَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ شَرِّ مَا صَنَعْتُ، أَبُوءُ لَكَ بِنِعْمَتِكَ عَلَيَّ، وَأَبُوءُ لَكَ بِذَنْبِي فَاغْفِرْ لِي، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَغْفِرُ الذُّنُوبَ إِلَّا أَنْتَ**

#### **Transliteration**
*Allahumma anta Rabbi la ilaha illa anta, khalaqtani wa ana abduka, wa ana 'ala 'ahdika wa wa'dika mastata'tu. A'udhu bika min sharri ma sana'tu, abu'u laka bini'matika 'alayya, wa abu'u laka bidhanbi faghfir li, fa-innahu la yaghfirudh-dhunuba illa anta.*

#### **Full English Translation**
> "O Allah, You are my Lord, none has the right to be worshipped but You. You created me and I am Your slave, and I am faithful to my covenant and my promise (to You) as much as I can. I seek refuge with You from all the evil I have done. I acknowledge before You all the blessings You have bestowed upon me, and I confess to You all my sins. So I entreat You to forgive my sins, for nobody can forgive sins except You."

#### **The Merit**
The Prophet ﷺ stated that **whoever recites this in the morning with firm conviction and dies on that same day before the evening will be among the people of Paradise.** Similarly, whoever recites it at night with conviction and dies before the morning will also enter Paradise.

***

### **Thematic Support from the Sources**

While the text above is from outside the provided materials, the sources strongly support the concepts contained within this supplication:

*   **Forgiveness as a Divine Attribute:** The du’a concludes by affirming that only Allah can forgive sins. This aligns with **Surah Al-i-'Imran (3:135)**, which asks rhetorically, "**and who can forgive sins except God?**" [1]. It also reflects the Divine Names **Al-Ghaffar** (The Repeatedly Forgiving) and **Al-Ghafur** (The Forgiving), describing Allah as One who "hides our wrong deeds" and "keeps forgiving us over and over" [2, 3].
*   **Morning and Evening Practice:** The requirement to say this du’a in the morning and evening matches the Quranic instruction in **Surah Ghafir (40:55)** to "**ask forgiveness for your sin and exalt [God] with praise of your Lord in the evening and the morning**" [4, 5].
*   **Acknowledging Servitude:** The du’a begins with the declaration of Tawhid and the admission of being a "slave" (*abduka*). The sources emphasize that **Ihsan** (perfection of faith) is to worship Allah as if you see Him, a state of complete devotion and awareness of His presence [6, 7].
*   **Conviction and Sincerity:** The merit of entering Paradise is tied to reciting the words with **conviction** (*Yaqin*). Sincerity (*Ikhlas*) is identified in the sources as a core condition of the Shahada, ensuring that worship is for Allah's sake alone [8, 9].

***

*Please note: The specific text and reference for Bukhari 6306 provided here are from external scholarly knowledge and are not contained in your current sources. You may wish to independently verify them. If you would like to find more narrations regarding seeking forgiveness or other morning and evening adhkar, I can initiate a search for additional sources.*

## Subtask 5 — Morning du'a for the day's good (Abu Dawud 5084 / Muslim 2723)

I have reviewed the provided sources, including the excerpts from Sahih Muslim and the Quranic translations. While the sources contain extensive information on the names of Allah, the pillars of faith, and various prayers, they do not include the specific chapters of **Sahih Muslim** (Volume 6, where Hadith 2723 is typically located) or the text of **Sunan Abu Dawud**.

However, as an expert in the field, I can provide the requested du'as from established Hadith literature. Please note that **the following texts and grades are not found in your provided sources** and should be independently verified.

### 1. The Du'a from Sahih Muslim (2723)
This is a comprehensive morning and evening remembrance. The version below is for the morning; in the evening, "Asbahna" (we have reached the morning) is replaced with "Amsayna" (we have reached the evening) and "al-yawm" (this day) with "al-laylah" (this night).

**Full Arabic:**
> أَصْبَحْنَا وَأَصْبَحَ الْمُلْكُ لِلَّهِ، وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، رَبِّ أَسْأَلُكَ خَيْرَ مَا فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ وَخَيْرَ مَا بَعْدَهُ، وَأَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ شَرِّ مَا فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ وَشَرِّ مَا بَعْدَهُ، رَبِّ أَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنَ الْكَسَلِ، وَسُوءِ الْكِبَرِ، رَبِّ أَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ عَذَابٍ فِي النَّارِ وَعَذَابٍ فِي الْقَبْرِ

**English Translation:**
> We have reached the morning and at this very time unto Allah belongs all sovereignty, and all praise is for Allah. There is no god but Allah, alone, without any partner. To Him belongs all sovereignty and His is all praise and He is over all things omnipotent. My Lord, I ask You for the good of this day and the good of what follows it, and I seek refuge in You from the evil of this day and the evil of what follows it. My Lord, I seek refuge in You from laziness and the evil of old age. My Lord, I seek refuge in You from the punishment of the Hell-fire and the punishment of the grave.

**Reference:** 
*   **Sahih Muslim**, Book 48 (The Book of Remembrance, Supplication, Repentance and Seeking Forgiveness), Hadith 2723.

**Grade:** 
*   **Sahih** (Authentic).

---

### 2. The Du'a from Abu Dawud (5084)
This prayer asks for specific blessings associated with the day’s activities.

**Full Arabic:**
> اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ خَيْرَ هَذَا الْيَوْمِ فَتْحَهُ، وَنَصْرَهُ، وَنُورَهُ، وَبَرَكَتَهُ، وَهُدَاهُ، وَأَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ شَرِّ مَا فِيهِ وَشَرِّ مَا بَعْدَهُ

**English Translation:**
> O Allah, I ask You for the good of this day: its victory, its support, its light, its blessings, and its guidance. And I seek refuge in You from the evil of what is in it and the evil of what follows it.

**Reference:** 
*   **Sunan Abi Dawud**, Book 43 (General Behavior), Hadith 5084.

**Grade:** 
*   Graded **Hasan** (Good) by some scholars and **Sahih** (Authentic) by others, such as Al-Albani in *Sahih Abi Dawud*.

---

### Insights from Your Provided Sources
While the full du'as are not in the provided excerpts, the **99 Names of Allah** and the **Quranic verses** in your sources explain the attributes invoked in these prayers:

*   **Al-Malik (The Sovereign King):** Both du'as acknowledge Allah's total control over the universe. As noted in the sources, Allah is the "real King of everything" [1]. The phrase *asbahal-mulku lillah* directly invokes this sovereignty.
*   **Al-Hadi (The Guide):** The request for "guidance" (*hudahu*) in the Abu Dawud narration appeals to Allah as the "GPS for your heart" who points toward goodness [2].
*   **An-Nafi (The Benefiter) and Ad-Darr (The Distresser):** The sources explain that Allah brings all good things and blessings [2], but also allows hard times for wise reasons [3]. These du'as are a practical application of seeking the *Naf'* (benefit/good) of the day and seeking refuge from its *Durr* (evil/harm).
*   **Morning and Evening Remembrance:** The sources highlight the Quranic command to "remember your Lord... in the mornings and the evenings" (Quran 7:205) and to "exalt Him morning and afternoon" (Quran 33:42) [4, 5].

Would you like me to use the discovery tool to search for further digital archives to verify the exact wording or check for other variants of these morning supplications?

## Subtask 6 — Evening adhkar between Asr and Maghrib (Amsayna)

The sources command and establish the practice of morning and evening remembrance through multiple Quranic ayahs and Sahih hadiths, emphasizing that such devotion provides protection and spiritual steadfastness.

### Quranic Commands for Morning and Evening Remembrance

The following verses from the sources explicitly command the believers to engage in the glorification and remembrance of Allah during the transitions of the day:

*   **Surah Al-Ahzab (33:41-42)**
    *   **English:** "O you who have believed, remember God with much remembrance And exalt Him morning and afternoon" [1].
    *   **Arabic:** يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا اذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ ذِكْرًا كَثِيرًا ۝ وَسَبِّحُوهُ بُكْرَةً وَأَصِيلًا *(Note: The Arabic text for this specific verse is not provided in the source excerpts and is included here from internal knowledge for completeness; you may wish to independently verify it.)*
*   **Surah Al-A’raf (7:205)**
    *   **English:** "And remember your Lord within yourself in humility and in fear without being apparent in speech - in the mornings and the evenings. And do not be among the heedless" [2].
    *   **Arabic:** وَاذْكُر رَّبَّكَ فِي نَفْسِكَ تَضَرُّعًا وَخِيفَةً وَدُونَ الْجَهْرِ مِنَ الْقَوْلِ بِالْغُدُوِّ وَالْآصَالِ وَلَا تَكُن مِّنَ الْغَافِلِينَ *(Note: The Arabic text for this specific verse is not provided in the source excerpts and is included here from internal knowledge for completeness; you may wish to independently verify it.)*
*   **Surah An-Nur (24:36)**
    *   **English:** "[Such niches are] in houses [i.e., mosques] which God has ordered to be raised and that His name be mentioned [i.e., praised] therein; exalting Him within them in the morning and the evenings" [3].
    *   **Arabic:** فِي بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ اللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا اسْمُهُ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُ فِيهَا بِالْغُدُوِّ وَالْآصَالِ *(Note: The Arabic text for this specific verse is not provided in the source excerpts and is included here from internal knowledge for completeness; you may wish to independently verify it.)*
*   **Surah Ar-Rum (30:17)**
    *   **English:** "So exalted is God when you reach the evening and when you reach the morning" [4].
*   **Surah Ghafir (40:55)**
    *   **Arabic:** فَاصْبِرْ إِنَّ وَعْدَ اللَّهِ حَقٌّ وَاسْتَغْفِرْ لِذَنبِكَ وَلِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَالْمُؤْمِنَاتِ [5].
    *   **English:** "So be patient, [O Muhammad]. Indeed, the promise of God is truth. And ask forgiveness for your sin and exalt [God] with praise of your Lord in the evening and the morning" [6].

### Sahih Hadiths Establishing Morning and Evening Adhkar

The sources highlight the specific merits of the morning and evening remembrances (*adhkar*), which serve as a "shield" and a means of protection from Satan [7, 8].

#### The Foundational Remembrance for Protection (Sahih Bukhari)
The sources provide a powerful dhikr to be recited daily for comprehensive protection:
*   **Hadith:** "If one says one-hundred times in one day: 'None has the right to be worshipped but Allah, the Alone Who has no partners, to Him belongs Dominion and to Him belong all the Praises, and He has power over all things (i.e. Omnipotent)', one will get the reward of manumitting ten slaves, and one-hundred good deeds will be written in his account, and one-hundred bad deeds will be wiped off or erased from his account, and **on that day he will be protected from the morning till evening from Satan**, and nobody will be superior to him except one who has done more than that which he has done" [8].
*   **Reference:** Sahih Bukhari, Volume 4, Book 54, Number 514 [8].
*   **Grade:** Sahih [8].

#### Evening Remembrance from Sahih Muslim
Regarding your request for the specific hadith from **Sahih Muslim 2723** (*Amsayna wa amsal-mulku lillah...*), please note that the **full text of this specific hadith is not present in the provided source excerpts**, as the Muslim collection in these sources concludes at hadith number 2089 [9].

However, the sources do confirm that the morning and evening *adhkar* are "prescribed Quranic and prophetic protections" that should be used to replace reliance on unauthentic objects like amulets [10]. The "mirror" effect you referred to is established by the practice of repeating morning supplications in the evening with the appropriate shift in time-reference (e.g., using "Amsayna"—we have reached the evening—instead of "Asbahna"—we have reached the morning).

#### Additional Sahih Adhkar from the Sources
*   **Seeking Refuge (The Mu'awwadhatayn):** The Prophet (ﷺ) stated that "wonderful verses have been sent down today, the like of which has never been seen! They are: 'Say: I seek refuge with the Lord of the dawn' (Surah Al-Falaq), and 'Say: I seek refuge with the Lord of men' (Surah An-Nas)" [11, 12]. Reciting these is a core part of the morning and evening routine for protection from evil [10].
*   **Protection Against Shirk:** The sources recommend incorporating a specific du'a into the daily morning and evening *adhkar* to protect against both major and minor shirk: "O Allah, I seek refuge in You from associating anything with You knowingly, and I seek Your forgiveness for what I do not know" [13, 14].

---

## Subtask 7 — Three Quls 3x morning and evening (Abu Dawud 5082)

The specific hadith you are requesting regarding the recitation of **Surah al-Ikhlas**, **al-Falaq**, and **al-Nas** three times in the morning and evening to "suffice you from everything" is recorded in the **Sunan of Abu Dawud** and **Jami' at-Tirmidhi**. While the provided sources contain English translations of these surahs [1-3] and mention the virtues of the "matchless verses" of protection (Mu'awwidhatayn) narrated by Uqbah ibn Amir in Sahih Muslim [4], the exact text of the hadith from Abu Dawud 5082 and the full Arabic text for Surahs 113 and 114 are not found within the provided excerpts. 

The following information regarding the hadith and the Arabic text of the surahs is provided from my general training data, and I recommend independent verification for these specific texts.

### **The Hadith**

*   **Arabic Text:** 
    عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ خُبَيْبٍ رضي الله عنه، قَالَ‏:‏ خَرَجْنَا فِي لَيْلَةِ مَطَرٍ وَظُلْمَةٍ شَدِيدَةٍ نَطْلُبُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِيُصَلِّيَ لَنَا، فَأَدْرَكْنَاهُ فَقَالَ‏:‏ ‏"‏قُلْ‏"‏‏.‏ فَلَمْ أَقُلْ شَيْئًا، ثُمَّ قَالَ‏:‏ ‏"‏قُلْ‏"‏‏.‏ فَلَمْ أَقُلْ شَيْئًا، ثُمَّ قَالَ‏:‏ ‏"‏قُلْ‏"‏‏.‏ فَقُلْتُ‏:‏ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، مَا أَقُولُ‏؟‏ قَالَ‏:‏ **‏"‏قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ، وَالْمُعَوِّذَتَيْنِ، حِينَ تُمْسِي وَحِينَ تُصْبِحُ ثَلاَثَ مَرَّاتٍ، تَكْفِيكَ مِنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ‏"‏‏.**
*   **English Translation:** 
    Abdullah ibn Khubayb reported: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to me, "**Recite 'Say: He is Allah, the One' (Surah Al-Ikhlas) and the Mu'awwidhatayn (Surah Al-Falaq and Surah An-Nas) three times in the morning and evening; they will suffice you from everything.**"
*   **Reference:** Sunan Abu Dawud (5082), Jami' at-Tirmidhi (3575), and Sunan an-Nasa'i (5428).
*   **Grade:** **Hasan Sahih** (Tirmidhi); **Sahih** (Al-Albani).

---

### **The Three Surahs (Al-Mu'awwidhat)**

Below is the text of the three surahs as found in the sources (where available) and from external knowledge.

#### **1. Surah Al-Ikhlas (112)**
*   **Arabic:** قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ ۝ اللَّهُ الصَّمَدُ ۝ لَمْ يَلِدْ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ ۝ وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌ [5]
*   **English:** 
    1. Say, "He is God, [who is] One,
    2. God, the Eternal Refuge.
    3. He neither begets nor is born,
    4. Nor is there to Him any equivalent." [1]

#### **2. Surah Al-Falaq (113)**
*   **Arabic:** قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ الْفَلَقِ ۝ مِنْ شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ ۝ وَمِنْ شَرِّ غَاسِقٍ إِذَا وَقَبَ ۝ وَمِنْ شَرِّ النَّفَّاثَاتِ فِي الْعُقَدِ ۝ وَمِنْ شَرِّ حَاسِدٍ إِذَا حَسَدَ
*   **English:** 
    1. Say, "I seek refuge in the Lord of daybreak
    2. From the evil of that which He created
    3. And from the evil of darkness when it settles
    4. And from the evil of the blowers in knots
    5. And from the evil of an envier when he envies." [2]

#### **3. Surah An-Nas (114)**
*   **Arabic:** قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ النَّاسِ ۝ مَلِكِ النَّاسِ ۝ إِلَهِ النَّاسِ ۝ مِنْ شَرِّ الْوَسْوَاسِ الْخَنَّاسِ ۝ الَّذِي يُوَسْوِسُ فِي صُدُورِ النَّاسِ ۝ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ
*   **English:** 
    1. Say, "I seek refuge in the Lord of mankind,
    2. The Sovereign of mankind,
    3. The God of mankind,
    4. From the evil of the retreating whisperer -
    5. Who whispers [evil] into the breasts of mankind -
    6. From among the jinn and mankind." [3]

### **Summary of Virtues from the Sources**
The sources emphasize that these verses are **matchless** and were revealed as a means of seeking refuge with God from all kinds of evil, including magic and envy [2, 4, 6]. The Prophet (peace be upon him) described Surah al-Ikhlas as being equivalent to **one-third of the Quran** [1]. Following the Prophet's instruction to remember the Lord "in the mornings and the evenings" [7] through these recitations is considered a primary way to secure divine protection [8].

## Subtask 8 — Ayat al-Kursi morning and evening (Bukhari 2311)

### Ayat al-Kursi (The Verse of the Throne)

Ayat al-Kursi is identified in the prophetic traditions as the **greatest verse in the Book of Allah** [1]. It establishes Allah's absolute sovereignty, His ever-living nature, and His total control over the universe [2].

**Arabic Text:**
اللَّهُ لَا إِلَٰهَ إِلَّا هُوَ الْحَيُّ الْقَيُّومُ ۚ لَا تَأْخُذُهُ سِنَةٌ وَلَا نَوْمٌ ۚ لَّهُ مَا فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَمَا فِي الْأَرْضِ ۗ مَن ذَا الَّذِي يَشْفَعُ عِندَهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ ۚ يَعْلَمُ مَا بَيْنَ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمَا خَلْفَهُمْ ۖ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِّنْ عِلْمِهِ إِلَّا بِمَا شَاءَ ۚ وَسِعَ كُرْسِيُّهُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ ۖ وَلَا يَئُودُهُ حِفْظُهُمَا ۚ وَهُوَ الْعَلِيُّ الْعَظِيمُ [3].

**English Translation:**
"Allah - there is no deity except Him, the Ever-Living, the Sustainer of [all] existence. Neither drowsiness overtakes Him nor sleep. To Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth. Who is it that can intercede with Him except by His permission? He knows what is [presently] before them and what will be after them, and they encompass not a thing of His knowledge except for what He wills. His Kursī extends over the heavens and the earth, and their preservation tires Him not. And He is the Most High, the Most Great" [4].

---

### Sahih Hadith on Protection from Satan (Shayatin)

The primary hadith establishing the protective nature of Ayat al-Kursi for the morning and evening is the narration of **Abu Hurayra and the thief** (who was Satan in disguise).

**Hadith Text (Summary):**
Abu Hurayra was appointed by the Prophet ﷺ to guard the Zakat of Ramadan. For three consecutive nights, a man came and stole handfuls of food. Each time, Abu Hurayra caught him, and each time the man made an excuse of poverty and need, leading Abu Hurayra to release him out of pity [5].

On the third night, when Abu Hurayra threatened to take him to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, the thief said: "I will teach you some words with which Allah will benefit you... **Whenever you go to bed, recite 'Ayat-al-Kursi'**... till you finish the whole verse. (If you do so), **Allah will appoint a guard for you who will stay with you and no satan will come near you till morning**" [5].

When Abu Hurayra informed the Prophet ﷺ the next morning, he ﷺ replied: **"He really spoke the truth, although he is an absolute liar. Do you know whom you were talking to, these three nights, O Abu Huraira? ... It was Satan"** [5, 6].

*   **Reference:** Sahih al-Bukhari 2311 (Volume 3, Book 36, Number 476/530) [5, 6].
*   **Grade:** Sahih [6].
*   **Significance:** While the hadith explicitly mentions sleep/nighttime protection, scholars and the sources suggest replacing reliance on physical amulets with these prescribed Quranic protections for the morning and evening (adhkar) to ensure constant divine guarding [7].

---

### Hadith on Entering Paradise

The sources and prophetic traditions also establish the virtue of reciting this verse after every obligatory (*fard*) prayer.

**Hadith Text:**
The Prophet ﷺ said: **"Whoever recites Ayat al-Kursi after every prescribed prayer, nothing prevents him from entering Paradise except death."**

*   **Reference:** This specific narration is found in **Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra** (Hadith 9848) and **Amal al-Yawm wa al-Layla** (Hadith 100), and is also recorded by **al-Tabarani** and **Ibn Hibban**.
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic) according to Al-Albani and Al-Arna'ut. 
*   **Note:** While this specific text is not found in the provided snippets of Sahih al-Bukhari or Sahih Muslim in your notebook, it is a well-documented Sahih hadith in the secondary Sahih collections (al-Sunan). The provided sources in the notebook do confirm that the Prophet ﷺ frequently sought refuge in Allah and taught his companions to recite specific verses for spiritual elevation and protection [1, 7].

---

## Subtask 9 — Ayat al-Kursi before sleep (Bukhari 2311)

The information you requested regarding the account of **Abu Hurayra and the thief** in the storehouse of zakat is found in **Sahih al-Bukhari**. The following details are drawn from the sources provided, with the Arabic text supplied from external knowledge to complete your request.

### **Sahih Hadith: Abu Hurayra and the Thief (Satan)**
This hadith is found in **Sahih al-Bukhari, Volume 3, Book 38, Number 505** (often cited as **2311** in modern numbering systems) [1, 2].

**Arabic Hadith Text:** 
(Note: The following Arabic text is provided from external knowledge as the source excerpts are in English.)
عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ سِيرِينَ، عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ـ رضى الله عنه ـ قَالَ وَكَّلَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِحِفْظِ زَكَاةِ رَمَضَانَ، فَأَتَانِي آتٍ، فَجَعَلَ يَحْثُو مِنَ الطَّعَامِ، فَأَخَذْتُهُ فَقُلْتُ لأَرْفَعَنَّكَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم‏.‏ ... فَقَالَ إِذَا أَوَيْتَ إِلَى فِرَاشِكَ فَاقْرَأْ آيَةَ الْكُرْسِيِّ لَنْ يَزَالَ عَلَيْكَ مِنَ اللَّهِ حَافِظٌ، وَلاَ يَقْرَبَكَ شَيْطَانٌ حَتَّى تُصْبِحَ‏.‏ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ‏"‏ صَدَقَكَ وَهُوَ كَذُوبٌ، ذَاكَ شَيْطَانٌ ‏"‏‏.

**Full English Translation:** 
"Narrated Abu Huraira: Allah's Apostle put me in charge of the Zakat of Ramadan (i.e. Zakat-ul-Fitr). Someone came to me and started scooping some of the foodstuff of (Zakat) with both hands. I caught him and told him that I would take him to Allah's Apostle." [2]. 

Abu Huraira relates that he caught the man three times; each time the man complained of great need and poverty, and Abu Huraira set him free out of pity [1]. On the third night, when Abu Huraira insisted on taking him to the Prophet ﷺ, the man said: **"Whenever you go to bed, recite 'Ayat-al-Kursi'—'Allahu la ilaha illa huwa-l-Haiy-ul Qaiyum' till you finish the whole verse. (If you do so), Allah will appoint a guard for you who will stay with you and no satan will come near you till morning."** [1]. 

Upon hearing this account the next morning, the Prophet ﷺ said: **"He really spoke the truth, although he is an absolute liar. Do you know whom you were talking to, these three nights, O Abu Huraira?"** Abu Huraira said, "No." The Prophet ﷺ said, **"It was Satan."** [1].

*   **Reference:** Sahih al-Bukhari, Vol. 3, Book 38, Hadith 505 (Modern: 2311).
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic).

---

### **Ayat al-Kursi (The Verse of the Throne)**
Reciting this verse before sleeping is established as a means of divine protection, as confirmed by the Prophet ﷺ in the hadith above.

**Arabic Text:**
(Note: The following Arabic text is provided from external knowledge to fulfill your request.)
اللَّهُ لَا إِلَٰهَ إِلَّا هُوَ الْحَيُّ الْقَيُّومُ ۚ لَا تَأْخُذُهُ سِنَةٌ وَلَا نَوْمٌ ۚ لَّهُ مَا فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَمَا فِي الْأَرْضِ ۗ مَن ذَا الَّذِي يَشْفَعُ عِندَهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ ۚ يَعْلَمُ مَا بَيْنَ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمَا خَلْفَهُمْ ۖ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِّنْ عِلْمِهِ إِلَّا بِمَا شَاءَ ۚ وَسِعَ كُرْسِيُّهُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ ۖ وَلَا يَئُودُهُ حِفْظُهُمَا ۚ وَهُوَ الْعَلِيُّ الْعَظِيمُ

**English Translation:**
"**God - there is no deity except Him, the Ever-Living, the Sustainer of [all] existence.** Neither drowsiness overtakes Him nor sleep. To Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth. Who is it that can intercede with Him except by His permission? He knows what is [presently] before them and what will be after them, and they encompass not a thing of His knowledge except for what He wills. **His Kursī extends over the heavens and the earth, and their preservation tires Him not. And He is the Most High, the Most Great.**" [3].

*   **Reference:** Quran 2:255.
*   **Significance:** This is considered the **greatest verse** in the Book of Allah [4]. It explicitly describes Allah's absolute sovereignty, His ever-watchful nature, and His total control over the universe [5].

The sources emphasize that this verse is the "litmus test" for monotheism, defining Allah's absolute independence (**As-Samad**) and His attribute of being **Al-Qayyum** (The Self-Subsisting/Sustainer) [5, 6].

- [95] (source `3b603e14…`): Surah al-Ikhlas (112) defines Allah's oneness and absolute independence, serving as the "litmus test" for monotheism. Ayat al-Kursi (2:255) describes His sovereignty, living nature, and total control over the universe. Reading these with tafsir allows you to move from mere recitation to a deep intellectual and spiritual absorption of His attributes.

- [122] (source `4f722378…`): of the narrators) said: At the end of Surah al-Kahf, but Hammam said: At the beginning of Surah al-Kahf.
- [123] (source `3b603e14…`): Surah al-Ikhlas (112) defines Allah's oneness and absolute independence, serving as the "litmus test" for monotheism. Ayat al-Kursi (2:255) describes His sovereignty, living nature, and total control over the universe. Reading these with tafsir allows you to move from mere recitation to a deep intellectual and spiritual absorption of His attributes.
- [124] (source `2b2fed2b…`): Quran 30:50

---

## Subtask 10 — Blow into palms with Quls and wipe body 3x before sleep (Bukhari 5017)

The specific text for **Sahih al-Bukhari 5017** is not contained within the provided excerpts; however, the Quranic surahs mentioned in the hadith and the practice of bedtime recitations are well-documented in the sources. The following hadith text and details are provided from external knowledge to fulfill your request, while the surahs are drawn directly from the sources.

### **Sahih al-Bukhari 5017**
**Note:** This hadith text and its grade are provided from external knowledge.

*   **Arabic Hadith Text:** عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ إِذَا أَوَى إِلَى فِرَاشِهِ كُلَّ لَيْلَةٍ جَمَعَ كَفَّيْهِ ثُمَّ نَفَثَ فِيهِمَا فَقَرَأَ فِيهِمَا ‏{‏قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ‏}‏ وَ‏{‏قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ الْفَلَقِ‏}‏ وَ‏{‏قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ النَّاسِ‏}‏ ثُمَّ يَمْسَحُ بِهِمَا مَا اسْتَطَاعَ مِنْ جَسَدِهِ يَبْدَأُ بِهِمَا عَلَى رَأْسِهِ وَوَجْهِهِ وَمَا أَقْبَلَ مِنْ جَسَدِهِ يَفْعَلُ ذَلِكَ ثَلاَثَ مَرَّاتٍ
*   **English Translation:** Narrated 'Aisha: Whenever the Prophet (ﷺ) went to bed every night, he used to **cup his hands together and blow into them** after reciting **Surah Al-Ikhlas, Surah Al-Falaq and Surah An-Nas**, and then **rub his hands over whatever parts of his body he was able to rub**, starting with his head, face and front of his body. He used to do that three times.
*   **Reference:** Sahih al-Bukhari, Book 66 (Virtues of the Qur'an), Hadith 5017.
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic).

---

### **The Three Surahs (The "Quls")**
The sources provide the full Arabic text and English translation for the three surahs mentioned in the hadith [1]. They are used for **purification of faith** and **seeking refuge from evil** [2-4].

#### **1. Surah al-Ikhlas (112: The Sincerity/Purification)**
This surah is described as being **equivalent to one-third of the Quran** [2, 5]. It defines Allah's oneness and absolute independence [6].
*   **Arabic:** بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَٰنِ الرَّحِيمِ . قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ . اللَّهُ الصَّمَدُ . لَمْ يَلِدْ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ . وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌ [2]
*   **English:** "In the Name of God, the Most Compassionate, the Most Merciful. 1. Say, 'He is God, [who is] One. 2. God, the Eternal Refuge. 3. He neither begets nor is born, 4. Nor is there to Him any equivalent.'" [2]

#### **2. Surah al-Falaq (113: The Daybreak)**
This surah is recited to **seek God’s protection from all kinds of evil**, specifically from darkness and those who practice magic [3, 7].
*   **Arabic:** بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَٰنِ الرَّحِيمِ . قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ الْفَلَقِ . مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ . وَمِن شَرِّ غَاسِقٍ إِذَا وَقَبَ . وَمِن شَرِّ النَّفَّاثَاتِ فِي الْعُقَدِ . وَمِن شَرِّ حَاسِدٍ إِذَا حَسَدَ [3]
*   **English:** "In the Name of God, the Most Compassionate, the Most Merciful. 1. Say, 'I seek refuge in the Lord of daybreak 2. From the evil of that which He created 3. And from the evil of darkness when it settles 4. And from the evil of the blowers in knots 5. And from the evil of an envier when he envies.'" [3]

#### **3. Surah an-Nas (114: Mankind)**
This surah is a prayer for refuge against the **retreating whisperer** (Satan) who whispers evil into the hearts of men [4].
*   **Arabic:** بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَٰنِ الرَّحِيمِ . قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ النَّاسِ . مَلِكِ النَّاسِ . إِلَٰهِ النَّاسِ . مِن شَرِّ الْوَسْوَاسِ الْخَنَّاسِ . الَّذِي يُوَسْوِسُ فِي صُدُورِ النَّاسِ . مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ [4]
*   **English:** "In the Name of God, the Most Compassionate, the Most Merciful. 1. Say, 'I seek refuge in the Lord of mankind, 2. The Sovereign of mankind, 3. The God of mankind, 4. From the evil of the retreating whisperer - 5. Who whispers [evil] into the breasts of mankind - 6. From among the jinn and mankind.'" [4]

### **Other Bedtime Traditions from the Sources**
*   **Surah al-Kafirun:** The Prophet ﷺ taught that reciting Surah al-Kafirun (109) before sleep provides **protection from polytheism** [8].
*   **Ayat al-Kursi:** Reciting Ayat al-Kursi (2:255) when going to bed ensures that **Allah appoints a guard** for the sleeper and no Satan will come near until morning [9].
*   **Tasbih, Tahmid, and Takbir:** The Prophet ﷺ advised Ali (RA) and Fatima (RA) to say **Subhan Allah (33x), Al-hamdu lillah (33x), and Allahu Akbar (34x)** when going to bed, stating it is better than having a servant [10].
*   **Specific Supplication:** Another bedtime sunnah involves performing wudu, lying on the right side, and reciting a specific du'a of surrender to Allah; if the person dies that night, they **die with faith** [11, 12].

- [182] (source `3b603e14…`): Surah al-Ikhlas (112) defines Allah's oneness and absolute independence, serving as the "litmus test" for monotheism. Ayat al-Kursi (2:255) describes His sovereignty, living nature, and total control over the universe. Reading these with tafsir allows you to move from mere recitation to a deep intellectual and spiritual absorption of His attributes.

## Subtask 11 — Surah al-Mulk before sleep (Tirmidhi 2891)

While the specific Arabic and English texts for the hadiths from **Sunan at-Tirmidhi 2891** and the narration regarding the title **"Al-Mani'ah"** (The Protector) are not explicitly contained in the provided excerpts, the sources provide the foundational Quranic text for Surah al-Mulk and extensive context regarding the **punishment of the grave** and the Prophet's ﷺ recitation habits.

The following information is provided based on the sources where available, supplemented by external knowledge for the specific hadith texts you requested.

### **Surah al-Mulk, Verse 1**
*   **Arabic Text:** تَبَارَكَ الَّذِي بِيَدِهِ الْمُلْكُ وَهُوَ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ [1]
*   **English Translation:** "Blessed is He in whose hand is dominion, and He is over all things competent." [1]
*   **Meaning:** This verse establishes that the entire universe is a "well organized and fortified Kingdom" belonging to Allah, who brought it into existence from nothing [2]. His power is infinite, and He is in total charge of every creature [2, 3].

---

### **Hadith 1: Recitation Before Sleep (External Knowledge)**
The hadith you referenced regarding the Prophet's ﷺ nightly routine is found in **Jami' at-Tirmidhi** (Hadith 2892, often indexed as 2891).

*   **Arabic Text:** عَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم لاَ يَنَامُ حَتَّى يَقْرَأَ ‏:‏ ‏(‏ الم تَنْزِيلُ ‏)‏ وَ ‏(‏ تَبَارَكَ الَّذِي بِيَدِهِ الْمُلْكُ ‏)
*   **English Translation:** Narrated by Jabir ibn Abdullah: "The Prophet ﷺ would not sleep until he had recited *Alif Lam Mim Tanzil* (Surah as-Sajdah) and *Tabarak alladhi bi yadihi'l-Mulk* (Surah al-Mulk)."
*   **Reference:** Jami' at-Tirmidhi, Book 45 (Virtues of the Quran), Hadith 2892.
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic) according to Al-Albani; others have graded it as **Hasan** (Good).

**Context from Sources:** While the sleep-specific hadith is external, the sources confirm that the Prophet ﷺ held **Surah as-Sajdah** (32) and **Surah al-Insan** (76) in high regard, frequently reciting them during the **Fajr prayer on Fridays** [4-6].

---

### **Hadith 2: Surah al-Mulk as 'The Protector' (External Knowledge)**
The narration regarding Surah al-Mulk’s intercession and its name **"Al-Mani'ah"** is widely reported in various collections.

*   **Arabic Text:** هِيَ الْمَانِعَةُ هِيَ الْمُنْجِيَةُ تُنْجِيهِ مِنْ عَذَابِ الْقَبْرِ
*   **English Translation:** "It is the Protector (*al-Mani'ah*), it is the Rescuer (*al-Munjiyah*); it rescues him from the punishment of the grave."
*   **Alternative Narration (Abu Huraira):** "A Surah from the Quran which has thirty verses will intercede for its reciter until he is forgiven: 'Blessed is He in whose hand is the dominion.'"
*   **Reference:** Sunan at-Tirmidhi (2890), Sunan Abu Dawud, and An-Nasa'i. 
*   **Grade:** **Hasan** (Good).

**Theological Support from Sources:**
The concept of seeking rescue from the grave is deeply embedded in the sources. The Prophet ﷺ warned that "you will be put to trials in your graves" [7] and described the grave as a place that can be "full of darkness" or "illuminated" by prayer [8, 9]. He strictly commanded his followers to **seek refuge from the punishment of the grave** in every prayer [10-13]. The role of Surah al-Mulk as a protector aligns with this consistent emphasis on divine aid against the "trials of the grave" [14, 15].

### **Summary of Benefits for the Reciter**
According to these traditions, a person who maintains the practice of reciting these Surahs—particularly Surah al-Mulk—obtains the following:
1.  **Divine Protection:** Reciting Quranic protections replaces reliance on unauthorized "amulets" or superstitious objects [16].
2.  **Intercession:** The Surah acts as a "pleader" for the reciter on the Day of Resurrection [17].
3.  **Safety from Torment:** It serves as a shield against the severe "torment of the grave" mentioned throughout the sources [11, 13].

***Note:** The hadith texts and specific grades above are from external Islamic literature as they are not present in your provided source excerpts. I recommend verifying them against a full copy of the referenced collections.*

---

## Subtask 12 — Sleep on right side, hand under cheek, facing qibla (Bukhari 6314)

The Sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ regarding sleeping posture, including lying on the right side and placing the hand under the cheek, is established in several **Sahih** hadiths found in both **Sahih al-Bukhari** and **Sahih Muslim**.

### 1. Lying on the Right Side (Bukhari 247 / 6314)
The Prophet ﷺ explicitly commanded lying on the right side when going to bed. This is part of a comprehensive bedtime routine that includes performing ablution (*wudu*).

*   **Arabic Text:** إِذَا أَتَيْتَ مَضْجَعَكَ فَتَوَضَّأْ وُضُوءَكَ لِلصَّلَاةِ ثُمَّ اضْطَجِعْ عَلَى شِقِّكَ الْأَيْمَنِ
*   **English Translation:** "Whenever you go to bed perform ablution like that for the prayer, **lie on your right side** and say: 'O Allah! I surrender to You and entrust all my affairs to You...'" [1].
*   **Reference:** Sahih al-Bukhari, Volume 1, Book 4, Number 247 (also found in Book 80, Hadith 6314).
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic).
*   **Note:** The sources confirm that this was also his practice during the short rest after the Sunnah of Fajr, where he would **"lie on his right side till the Mu'adhdhin came"** [2-5].

### 2. Placing the Right Hand Under the Cheek (Muslim 1453)
The sources describe the Prophet ﷺ supporting his head with his hand while lying on his right side.

*   **Arabic Text:** كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا كَانَ فِي سَفَرٍ فَعَرَّسَ بِلَيْلٍ اضْطَجَعَ عَلَى يَمِينِهِ وَإِذَا عَرَّسَ قُبَيْلَ الصُّبْحِ نَصَبَ ذِرَاعَهُ وَوَضَعَ رَأْسَهُ عَلَى كَفِّهِ
*   **English Translation:** "When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was on a journey and got down for rest at night, he used to **lie down on his right side**, and when he lay down for rest before the dawn, he used to stretch his forearm and **place his head over his palm**" [6].
*   **Reference:** Sahih Muslim, Book 4, Number 1453 (also reported in Bukhari 6314 with the phrasing "placing his right hand under his right cheek").
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic).

### 3. Facing the Qibla
While the provided sources emphasize lying on the right side, they do not contain a specific Sahih hadith explicitly commanding facing the Qibla *for sleep* in the same way they command the right-side posture. However, the sources establish the **Ka'bah as the Qibla** for all believers [7] and describe the Prophet ﷺ praying toward the Qibla while his wives lay in front of him on the bed [8-11]. 

*(Note: The scholarly tradition of facing the Qibla while sleeping on the right side—mimicking the posture of the deceased in the grave—is widely practiced in the Sunnah but is not explicitly detailed as a command in the specific hadith snippets provided.)*

### Summary of the Sleeping Sunnah from the Sources:
1.  **Ablution:** Perform wudu as if for prayer before bed [1].
2.  **Right Side:** Lie down specifically on the right side [1, 6].
3.  **Hand Placement:** Support the head with the palm or place the hand under the cheek [6].
4.  **Supplication:** Recite the specific *du'a* of surrender and faith as the last utterance of the night [1].
5.  **Spiritual Health:** By following this posture and reciting the *du'a*, the Prophet ﷺ stated that **"if you die on that very night, you will die with faith"** [12].

**Disclaimer:** The Arabic text for these hadiths and the specific mention of facing the Qibla are provided from external knowledge to complete your request, as the source excerpts provided are primarily English translations and do not include the full Arabic text for these specific narrations.

## Subtask 13 — Final words before sleep: 'Bismika Allahumma amutu wa ahya' (Bukhari 6314)

The specific text for **Sahih Bukhari 6314** is not contained within the provided excerpts (which primarily cover Sahih Bukhari through Volume 6 and specific thematic selections). However, the supplications requested are well-established in the Sahih literature and are conceptually supported by the Quranic verses and names of Allah found in your sources.

The following information regarding the hadith is provided from external knowledge to fulfill your request:

### **Sahih Hadith: The Prophet's ﷺ Supplications for Sleep and Waking**
This hadith is narrated on the authority of **Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman** (and also narrated by Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib in related entries).

*   **Supplication Before Sleep:**
    *   **Arabic:** بِاسْمِكَ اللَّهُمَّ أَمُوتُ وَأَحْيَا
    *   **English:** "In Your name, O Allah, I die and I live."
*   **Supplication Upon Waking:**
    *   **Arabic:** الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِي أَحْيَانَا بَعْدَ مَا أَمَاتَنَا وَإِلَيْهِ النُّشُورُ
    *   **English:** "All praise is for Allah who gave us life after having taken it from us (death/sleep), and unto Him is the resurrection."
*   **Reference:** **Sahih al-Bukhari 6314** (and **6324**).
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic).

**Note:** As this specific hadith text is from outside the provided source excerpts, you may wish to independently verify it.

---

### **Theological Foundations from the Sources**
While the direct hadith text was missing, your sources provide deep context for why these specific words are used:

1.  **Sleep as a "Minor Death":** The sources quote **Surah al-An'am (6:60)**, which states that Allah **"takes your souls by night"** and then **"revives you therein [by day] that a specified term may be fulfilled"** [1]. Similarly, **Surah az-Zumar (39:42)** confirms that Allah takes the souls at the time of death and during sleep, keeping those decreed to die and releasing others [2].
2.  **Day as Resurrection:** The waking du'a concludes with the phrase "unto Him is the resurrection." This aligns with **Surah al-Furqan (25:47)**, which explains that Allah **"has made the night for you as clothing and sleep [a means for] rest and has made the day a resurrection"** [3].
3.  **The Attributes of Allah:**
    *   **Al-Muhyi (The Giver of Life):** The sources explain that Allah gives life to everything, including the "beating heart," and will one day bring every person back to life [4].
    *   **Al-Mumit (The Taker of Life):** This attribute reflects the portion of the du'a stating "I die," as Allah decides when every living thing's life ends [5].
    *   **Al-Hayy (The Ever-Living):** Unlike humans who sleep (the minor death), Allah **"never gets old, never sleeps, and never goes away"** [5, 6].
4.  **Prophetic Practice:** The sources describe the Prophet's ﷺ habit of waking in the middle of the night, sitting up, and **"rubbing the traces of sleep off his face with his hands"** before reciting the concluding verses of Surah Aal-Imran [7-9].

If you would like me to conduct a broader search for other morning and evening supplications found in the later volumes of Sahih Bukhari or other collections not currently in the notebook, I can call the **discover_sources** tool. Would you like me to do that?

## Subtask 14 — Pre-Dhuhr transition: praying at first/proper time (Quran 4:103, Bukhari 527)

### **Quranic Decree on Prayer Times**

The Quran establishes the five daily prayers as an obligation tied to specific periods of the day, emphasizing that they cannot be performed at one's own leisure but must follow a divine schedule.

*   **Arabic Text:** إِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ كَانَتْ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ كِتَابًا مَّوْقُوتًا
*   **English Translation:** "**Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers a decree of specified times.**" [1], [2], [3]
*   **Reference:** Quran 4:103.

This verse serves as the foundation for the "guarding" of prayers (*muhafadhah*), which implies **consistent vigilance** over these times [4]. The sources describe this as a **sacred duty** inextricably linked to the rotation of the day [5]. Other verses further define these windows, such as the command to establish prayer at the **"decline of the sun"** until the **"darkness of the night"** and specifically the **"Quran at dawn,"** which is uniquely witnessed by angels [6], [7].

***

### **The Merit of Praying at the Earliest Time**

The specific virtue of performing these prayers at the beginning of their allotted windows (*awwal al-waqt*) is established in several Sahih narrations from the companion **Abdullah ibn Mas'ud**.

**Sahih Hadith: The Dearest Deed**
*   **Arabic Text:** سَأَلْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: أَيُّ الْعَمَلِ أَحَبُّ إِلَى اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ: **«الصَّلَاةُ عَلَى وَقْتِهَا»**
*   **English Translation:** Abdullah ibn Mas'ud narrated: "I asked the Prophet (ﷺ), '**Which deed is the best (or dearest to Allah)?**' He replied, '**To offer the prayers at their early stated fixed times.**' I asked, 'What is the next (in goodness)?' He replied, 'To be good and dutiful to your parents.' I again asked, 'What is the next?' He replied, 'To participate in Jihad in Allah's Cause.'" [8], [9], [10]
*   **Full References:** Sahih al-Bukhari 527 (also Vol. 1, Book 10, No. 505); Sunan at-Tirmidhi 170; Sahih Muslim 85 (Book 1, No. 0151) [11].
*   **Grade:** **Sahih** (Authentic) [10].

***

### **Scholarly Insights and Practice**

The requirement to pray at specified times was revealed during the **Night Journey (Isra and Mi'raj)**, where initially fifty prayers were decreed and subsequently reduced to five, with the promise that these five would carry the reward of fifty [12], [13]. The Angel Gabriel personally demonstrated the start and end of each prayer window to the Prophet ﷺ over the course of two days to define the "limits" of the time [14].

**Spiritual Significance:**
*   **Prompt Response:** Praying early is viewed as an **urgent response** to Allah's call, similar to how the righteous companions would call upon Allah immediately when a calamity struck [15], [10].
*   **Demonstration of Love:** Performing the prayer at its earliest time demonstrates an **eagerness to meet Allah** and ensures that worldly obligations do not eventually crowd the prayer out of its window [16].
*   **Divine Testimony:** The morning prayer is highlighted as being **"ever witnessed"** by the angels of both the night and the day as they take their turns in succession [17], [18], [19].

The Prophet ﷺ warned against the strategy of the devil, who attempts to make a person **lazy or forgetful** of the prayer times [20], [21]. Abandonment of these specified prayers is described in the sources as the barrier between a person and disbelief [22]. To protect the integrity of the prayer, believers are encouraged to treat the Adhan as a **hard deadline** rather than a suggestion, aiming to begin the prayer within fifteen minutes of the call [16].
